**GT:** `-0.752289977167006*v*(1 - x**2) - 0.61401597703647*v - 0.307007988518235*v*exp(-Abs(x)) - 1.1598282332023*x**3`

Expanding: `0.752289977167006*v*x**2 - 0.752289977167006*v - 0.61401597703647*v - 0.307007988518235*v*exp(-Abs(x)) - 1.1598282332023*x**3`

Simplifying: `0.752289977167006*v*x**2 - 1.36630595420348*v - 0.307007988518235*v*exp(-Abs(x)) - 1.1598282332023*x**3`

So GT = `c_a*v*x**2 + c_b*x**3 + c_c*v + c_d*v*exp(-|x|)`

The key challenge is the `exp(-|x|)` term. Most candidates have `exp(c*x)` which is NOT the same as `exp(-|x|)` since `exp(-|x|)` is not an exponential of a linear function of x (it's piecewise: `exp(-x)` for x>0 and `exp(x)` for x<0).

**Critical observation:** `exp(-|x|)` cannot be represented as `exp(c*x)` for any constant c. So any candidate relying solely on `exp(c*x)` to capture this term will fail.

Let me check candidates that might have alternative structures:

- **Candidate 33:** `c0*v*x**2 + c1*x**3 + c2*v + c3*v*exp(c4*x)` — Cannot match exp(-|x|).

- **Candidate 2:** Has `v*x**c3` and `v*x**c5*exp(c6*x)` — these can't produce exp(-|x|).

- **Candidate 34:** Has `v*(c6 + x)**c7` — a power function, not exp(-|x|).

- **Candidate 39:** Has `x**c4` (not multiplied by v) — doesn't help.

- **Candidate 59:** Has `v*exp(c6*x**2)` — this is exp of x², not |x|.

None of the exponential terms `exp(c*x)` can reproduce `exp(-|x|)` because `exp(-|x|)` is symmetric (even function) while `exp(c*x)` is neither even nor odd (unless c=0, giving constant 1).

Let me check if any candidate has enough structure to approximate exp(-|x|) exactly through some algebraic identity... No standard algebraic combination of the offered terms (polynomials, exp(cx), sin, cos, log, sqrt, powers) can exactly equal exp(-|x|) for all x.

Could any candidate avoid needing exp(-|x|) by having it built from other components? The function exp(-|x|) is non-analytic at x=0, so it cannot be represented by any finite combination of analytic functions. Most candidate terms (polynomials, exp(cx), sin, cos, log of analytic expressions, powers) are analytic everywhere or on large domains. 

However, candidates with `sqrt(c + x)` introduce non-analyticity. Let me check candidate 6: `c0*v*x**2 + c1*x**3 + c2*v + c3*v*sqrt(c4 + x) + c5*v*exp(c6*x)`. The sqrt term is non-analytic at x = -c4, but sqrt(c4+x) ≠ exp(-|x|) for any parameter choice.

Candidate 51: `c3*v*sqrt(c4 + x) + c5*v*x**c6*exp(c7*x)` — still can't produce exp(-|x|).

Candidate 48: `c3*v**c4` — if c4=1, this is just c3*v, a constant multiple.

No candidate formula can produce `exp(-|x|)` since it requires a non-analytic, even function with a kink at x=0, and none of the available building blocks can create this.

After careful analysis of all 61 candidates, none can exactly match the GT due to the `exp(-Abs(x))` term which cannot be represented by any of the functional forms available in the candidates.
